Local News II

Jinliyuan Warehouse 133

Major Fire This Morning: At about 1:15 a.m. this morning (the 15th), a fire was reported at the Jinliyuan Warehouse No. 8 of the China Merchants Bureau on the Bund outside the French Concession's Xin Kaihe. Upon hearing the news, the reporter rushed to the scene and found smoke billowing into the sky. More than a dozen fire trucks and dozens of firefighters were working hard to extinguish the fire. However, the warehouse was full of goods and the doors and windows were tightly closed, making it difficult to extinguish the fire. Firefighters on the west side used axes to forcefully cut open four or five of the lower-level iron windows, causing thick smoke to pour out and rise into the sky. They diligently inserted nozzles to pour water, showing great courage. The reporter inquired about the cause of the fire, but opinions differed, making it difficult to determine the truth. However, the theory that a worker had carelessly left a cigarette fire was considered the most likely. It was confirmed that the fire was discovered at about 1:15 a.m. this morning. Initially, a dock patrolman noticed thick smoke coming from Warehouse No. 1 and knew something was wrong. He immediately reported it to the fire brigade, which dispatched fire trucks to extinguish the fire. However, it was predicted that the fire had been brewing inside the warehouse for a long time. According to people at the fire brigade, the warehouse was full of tobacco leaves, grains, and porcelain. There were a total of twenty-one warehouses, all of which were old-style buildings that had not been paved with terrazzo. However, each warehouse had a very strong wall separating it, preventing the fire from spreading. Firefighters said that the fire could not be extinguished until 9 or 10 a.m. When the reporter left the scene of the fire, the smoke was as black as ink, and the fire was still raging.

Record of a Madman's Suicide Attempt 134

Wounded But Saved: At about 10:30 a.m. yesterday, a madman about 40 years old, wearing a gray lined jacket and trousers, yellow socks, and no shoes, suddenly appeared at the Shunhe pawnshop entrance of the Baxianqiao Small Vegetable Market on the Route Cardinal Mercier in the French Concession. He was holding a sharp blade and waving it wildly in the street. Suddenly, he slashed his own head with the knife, causing blood to flow like a waterfall. However, his trachea and esophagus were not severed, so he continued to scream. The patrolmen there seized the blade, hired a car to take him to the police station, and then transferred him to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that his injuries were severe, but he could still be saved.

A Pair of Russian Lovers

Die Under Gunfire 135

First Murdered His Mistress, Then Committed Suicide: The Reason Was That the Woman Had a New Lover. At about 9 a.m. yesterday, Mrs. Damo, a divorced Russian woman residing at No. 624 Route des Peres, was shot in the heart by her lover, Granovsky, and died in her bedroom. Afterward, Granovsky returned to his own residence on Rue Luber and shot himself in the head, committing suicide. A pair of lovers ended their karma with two ruthless bullets. It is said that Granovsky and the woman had been in love for four years. Three years ago, the woman divorced her husband in Jinan, and Granovsky abandoned his wife in Qingdao and brought the woman to Shanghai. They then opened a dormitory on Rue Luber, and later added another one on Route des Peres, which the woman helped him manage. When the incident occurred this morning, the woman was preparing breakfast alone in her room. Her daughter had gone to work somewhere in the International Settlement. Granovsky broke into the room and killed her before leaving. It is said that the woman had invited Granovsky to breakfast this morning, but seeing him break down the door and enter in anger, it seemed that he was not coming to the appointment. It is also said that the two had recently been on bad terms, and it was rumored that the woman now had another lover, so the motive for the case may have been jealousy. The Russian woman was 37 years old and left behind a 17-year-old daughter. Granovsky was originally quite wealthy, having purchased land and opened several dormitories in Qingdao, but now most of his assets have been squandered. He left behind a wife and three sons.

Assassination of Inspector An Case

Liangxi Hotel Owner Released on Bail 141

The court ruled against the transfer. After Inspector An Zhendong of the Fourth District was assassinated, the Public Security Bureau arrested Wang Yaoting, who confessed that Li Maolin, the owner of the Liangxi Hotel on Hubei Road, who was from Wuxi, was the instigator. The bureau and the police station detained Li and brought him to the Special District District Court. The court ordered evidence to be presented for further investigation, as previously reported. Yesterday morning, Court President Zhou continued the interrogation. The defendant's lawyer, Fan Gang, submitted a letter from the Wuxi Fellow-Provincials Association proving that Li Maolin was a legitimate businessman. Court President Zhou then asked Qi Haitian, an official from the Public Security Bureau, whether there were any other witnesses besides Wang Yaoting in the case. Qi shook his head and said no, and requested permission to transfer the case. However, the police station's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, still opposed the transfer, saying that Wang Yaoting's confession was very vague. He said that Wang claimed that the two accomplices who went with him to commit the assassination were unknown, which was absurd in such a major case of murder. He also said that if Li gave Wang 100 yuan at the intersection of the Fourth Road, why did Li not pay him in a secluded hotel but in a public place, as if he deliberately wanted people to see it? Furthermore, he claimed not to know the date of An's assassination or the reason for the assassination. How could he not know the reason for killing a person, especially in such a serious case? Even when killing a chicken or dog, there is a reason. If he killed him, how could he not know the reason? He also claimed that An was sitting in a rickshaw at the time, but the investigation revealed that he was riding a bicycle when the incident occurred. All of this proves that Wang Yaoting's confession is not credible. If the transfer is approved based solely on this evidence, it would violate the purpose of protecting the lives and property of the people. If the Public Security Bureau has no sufficient evidence to present, we can only request his release, as Li has already been detained for a week. Lawyer Fan Gang then defended Li. Since the Public Security Bureau had stated that there was no other evidence, Court President Zhou ruled that the evidence was insufficient and did not approve the transfer. He ordered Li Maolin to pay 1,000 yuan bail for his release. If the Public Security Bureau has sufficient evidence to present, the case will be reviewed again.

After Being Dismissed, He Joined Bandits 142

Cui Zuoqing Arrested and His Accomplice Arrested: Cui Zuoqing, a native of Jiangbei who was formerly a detective in the Public Security Bureau of Kunshan County, came to Shanghai and joined bandits after being dismissed. Complicated Kidnapping Case 143

Wang Xie Shi, a woman from Jiangbei, used to live in a thatched house in Caozha, west of the Nanshi District Court. Because the Chinese police authorities ordered all thatched houses there to be moved to prevent fires, Xie Shi moved to a place near the New Public Office in Gaochang Temple on the 10th of this month. At 2 p.m. that day, she first took her six-year-old daughter, Mao Yatou, and some sundries to the new house. When she returned for the second load, Mao Yatou suddenly disappeared. She immediately searched everywhere but could not find her. A neighbor secretly told her that Huang Wenkai, a resident of the area, was a major suspect. Xie Shi then brought Huang to the Second District Police Station. After questioning by District Chief Wang, the case was turned over to the District Court because it involved the kidnapping of a child. Until yesterday, Liu Desheng (30 years old, from Haizhou), a cousin of Mao Yatou, heard that his cousin had disappeared and inquired everywhere. He was told that Gong Huang Shi (40 years old), a widow from Fuzhou who lived at No. 4, Lane 74, Jiangbian Road, Gaochang Temple, was trafficking in children. Liu broke into Huang's house and searched it thoroughly. He found a Jiangbei girl about 10 years old lying on the bed. She claimed to be Liu Meixi, 12 years old, and said that her home was on the loft above the bed shop near Taiping Bridge. She said that her mother was friends with Huang and that she had only come to stay temporarily yesterday. Last night, she saw another woman leading out a girl about 5 or 6 years old with cropped hair. Liu became even more suspicious and brought Huang and Liu Meixi to the Second District Police Station. After questioning by District Chief Wang, Huang confessed that she had bought Meixi a few days ago for 130 yuan as an adopted daughter. District Chief Wang saw that her words did not match what Meixi said and suspected that there was something wrong. He prepared a document and sent them to the court for processing. At the same time, Chen Jiabiao (34 years old, from Yancheng), a friend of Liu Desheng, heard that Liu had arrested Gong Shi and rushed to Gong's house. There was no one at home. He suddenly found a girl about 6 or 7 years old behind Gong's toilet. He questioned her, and she claimed to be Zeng Xingzi, 7 years old. Her father's name was Lao Qiang, her uncle's name was Xiao Laohu, she was very tall, her older sister's name was A Yi, and her younger sister's name was A Mei. They lived upstairs at Hezi Dian. She could not provide any other information. Chen took her out and happened to pass the entrance of the Second District Police Station, where Liu Desheng and others were preparing to take her to court. Chen handed Zeng Xingzi over to Liu and took her to the police station. Gong Shi kept evading questions. District Chief Wang prepared a document and sent her to the court for strict handling.

YWCA News 145

Children's Health Society: The YWCA Children's Health Society was suspended for several months due to financial difficulties after last winter's competition, but the community's desire for it has grown stronger. It is reported that the society has worked hard to support itself and has hired Ms. Chen Xiuyun, a kind and experienced female nurse, to take on the duties of the society, which will surely make a contribution. Since the beginning of spring, it has been actively preparing and has invited medical giants and social celebrities such as Fu Wenshou, Sun Keji, and Niu Huisheng, as well as Dr. Wu Weide and Mr. Li Yuanxin, to form a committee to design and implement the program. Female doctors Lin Ju'e, Yang Suolan, Su Shouzhen, and Liu Fulin are responsible for the examination. It is now scheduled that Tuesdays and Fridays will be the inspection days. Every Tuesday from 10 a.m. to 12 p.m. at the association's location at 26 Nanking Road, and every Friday from 10 a.m. to 12 p.m. at the association's dormitory on Rue de Ste Lucie. All children from one month to ten years old can register with the association's membership department, and all expenses are free, and they can obtain new methods of health.

Members' Regular Meeting: The association's membership department believes that there have been few opportunities to contact other associations in the past, which has created a sense of isolation. Therefore, the department has recently made efforts to improve this, doing everything possible for the members. For young women, there are tutoring classes. For working women, there is the Vocational Comrades Society. For mothers, there is the Children's Health Society. For homemakers, there are cooking classes, family associations, discussion groups, and travel and recreation activities, all of which are intended to promote moral, intellectual, physical, and aesthetic education. Recently, it has been decided that the members' regular meeting will be held every Tuesday from 4 p.m. to 5 p.m. There are various entertainment methods to help, and all members can bring their relatives and friends to the meeting. Chinese women have traditionally lacked community life. Let's work together to improve this.

Careless Fire at Old White Ferry in Pudong 146

Yesterday morning at 2:40 AM, a thatched house belonging to Chen Yujin, a native of Yancheng, Jiangsu Province, residing in the grass mudflat area of Old White Ferry in Pudong, caught fire due to negligence. The house, constructed of bamboo and rice straw, ignited quickly, and the flames spread rapidly. Chen and his family were awakened from their sleep and escaped in their underwear, narrowly avoiding danger. A patrolling police officer spotted the fire and blew his whistle. Soon after, Yang Zhongquan, the head of the First Precinct of the Third District, arrived with Deputy Inspectors Duan and Tong, along with senior officers, to maintain order. They immediately directed fire hoses to the scene to extinguish the blaze. However, their efforts were insufficient, and the fire continued to burn until 3:30 AM before it was finally extinguished. A total of sixteen thatched houses belonging to neighboring residents were destroyed. The residents in the area were mostly poor migrants who were left homeless after the fire, gathering near the scene, weeping pitifully. Afterwards, Officer Yang ordered Chen Yujin, who was suspected of starting the fire, to be taken to the station for questioning. Chen claimed that he was fast asleep when the fire started and had no idea how it began. However, the station's investigation revealed two possible causes: (1) Chen's wife was ill and was brewing medicine at the time, and a stray ember may have caused the fire; (2) A neighbor surnamed Yan was cooking a midnight meal, and it may have caused the fire. However, it was discovered that Yan had been away from home for a week, making the second theory less likely. Officer Yang ordered Chen to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation and to promptly handle the aftermath to prevent the disaster victims from becoming homeless.

Further Investigation into the Robbery on Fangbang Road 147

A youth emerged from an empty house, and after interrogation, the remaining robbers were pursued. At 7:20 PM the night before, the home of Li Gentao, a resident of Lane Lianqing, No. 23, Fangbang Road in the South City, was robbed by five people. Two patrol officers, Wang Yucai and Wang Ganqing, from the First Precinct of the Second District, apprehended one robber at the entrance of Kongjia Lane, recovering a pistol. The remaining robbers escaped without a trace. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. After the incident, Xu, the head of the Second District Precinct, immediately instructed patrolling officers in the area near the scene to be extra vigilant and to immediately inspect anyone acting suspiciously without any leniency. By around 1:30 AM the following morning, patrol officer Yu Jieqing from Post No. 31 and patrol officer Wang Ye from Post No. 30 noticed a youth rushing out of the empty house at No. 8 Honglan Gan Road in a panic, behaving suspiciously. The two officers stealthily followed him, observing his movements. They saw the youth enter a small congee shop on Zhaojia Road, pretending to eat, but his unease was evident in his demeanor. As the officers approached to inspect him, the youth pulled out a wooden-handled pistol and fired two shots at them. The officers returned fire with two shots, but both missed. The youth then fled, and the officers gave chase. The pursuit led them to Xicang Road, within the jurisdiction of the Third Precinct of the Second District, where patrol officers Chen Shouzheng and Li Xingbang from Posts No. 47 and No. 48 joined the pursuit. The robber was apprehended on the spot and taken to the Second District Precinct. Xu, the head of the precinct, arrived at the Second District Precinct after hearing the news and took the suspect and the pistol back for questioning. The suspect confessed to being Li Hongjun, 28 years old, from Hebei Province, and admitted to conspiring with others, including Zhang, Guo Yifa (Guo Xiaoshou), and Chen Tianhai, to commit robbery. He also revealed that they had gathered at the First Spring restaurant on Nanyang Bridge that afternoon, and that the gun belonged to Zhang. Zhang's address was uncertain, but Guo was currently residing at No. 31 Yuqing Lane, Observatory Road, in the French Concession, and the Huidong Inn on Xizilaihuo Street, Avenue Foch. Officer Xu ordered Inspector Zhang Yude to lead several senior officers, accompanied by French police, to the Huidong Inn, but the robbers had already fled. They then went to Observatory Road and apprehended Guo's wife, Guo Gongshi, who stated that she was 34 years old and knew nothing about her husband's actions. Officer Xu, based on the confession, sent the suspect, along with a wooden box pistol No. 48568 and two bullets, to the General Bureau for review.

Yijin Grass Cures Pulmonary Tuberculosis 151

Mr. Wang, residing at No. 113 Xintianxiang Lane, Yuanle Road, in this city, had been suffering from pulmonary tuberculosis for fifteen years. It would flare up periodically, and the condition worsened this past spring, almost becoming fatal. An X-ray taken at Renji Hospital revealed severe damage to his left lung. Both Chinese and Western doctors were helpless. He was persuaded to take Yijin Grass from the Peisheng Company on Zhonghua Road for over a month, and it miraculously saved him. Not only has there been no relapse to date, but his health has also improved. It is said that this grass has a radical curative effect on pulmonary tuberculosis, as proven by the Central Testing Institute, Dr. Lin Wu, a famous doctor, and Dr. Ye Boyang of Baolong Hospital.

Gansu Disaster Relief Association Established 153

Yesterday, Zhu Qinglan hosted a banquet at Yipinxian Restaurant. Gansu has suffered from continuous natural disasters and human calamities for years. Statistics show that more than three million people have died, and the people are displaced and impoverished, desperately in need of relief. Yang Jingzhou, Fan Liuqiao, Nie Zhenxuan, and other fellow Gansu natives living in Shanghai hosted a banquet at Yipinxian Restaurant yesterday for Zhu Qinglan, Chairman of the North China Relief Committee, and Wang Yiting, Cha Liangzhao, and others, requesting them to find ways to provide relief. In addition to Zhu, Wang, and Cha, more than twenty people attended, including Wu Zhihao, Huang Jingwan, and Xie Fusheng. Guo Zifan, the chairman, first reported the situation, followed by Long Youtian, a Gansu education inspector, who described the witnessed disaster in Gansu in detail, which was unbearable to hear. Zhu Qinglan and Wang Yiting then gave their replies, stating that they would treat the Gansu disaster equally and do their best to find ways to provide relief. Finally, the meeting discussed the establishment of the Shanghai Gansu Disaster Relief Association and publicly elected Guo Zifan as the resident director in Shanghai and Yang Jingzhou as the relief assistance committee member, who would begin work immediately.

Letter Requesting Strict Prevention of Fake Donation Drives 162

Hu Chongji is bold and reckless, Lü Bichou, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, wrote to Nie Lusheng: Mr. Lusheng, I am writing to inform you that I recently received a letter from Shanghai Guanghua Petroleum Co., Ltd., stating that Hu Chongji, a counselor from the 8th Division Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, fabricated a letter in Shanghai to solicit funds for the Revolutionary Orphans Education and Care Institute. The letter requested information if they were being dispatched by their department and sent the original letter for your review and reply. The Revolutionary Orphans Education and Care Institute is directly subordinate to the National Government, and all expenses are borne by the National Government. There is no connection with the institute, and we have never heard of anyone being assigned to solicit donations abroad. Hu Chongji fabricated the letter and misspelled his name, obviously impersonating and deceiving. If he comes to your company again, please immediately notify the garrison headquarters or the Public Security Bureau by telephone to arrest him for investigation, etc., in response. If the truth is not clear, the forged points are exposed to serve as a distinction. Upon investigation, the institute's official stationery always has the name of the organization printed in the lower corner of the last line, while the forged stationery has the name of the organization printed on top, and the character for Bichou in the word "宓种" is misspelled. Various flaws prove that the writing in the forged letter matches that of Hu Muzhou, who was also in Shanghai to solicit donations for the Hunan disaster last year, impersonating the Bichou letter. It is likely that Hu Chongji is a pseudonym for Hu Muzhou. The two are similar in repeatedly fabricating fraud and scams. Bichou has sent letters and telegrams to Shanghai officials requesting a thorough investigation and arrest, but he has not yet been apprehended. In addition to requesting the garrison headquarters and the municipal government to secretly investigate and handle the case, I will also send a photo of the forged letter along with the letter for your inspection and hope that you will take the time to convey it to the local wealthy merchants and widely publicize it so that they will not be deceived again. I am deeply grateful for this. Please accept my greetings, Lü Bichou's letter.

Dispute over Collection of House Tax Based on Estimated Value 163

The Taxpayers Association Sent a Letter Requesting Calculation Based on Actual Rent. According to the National News Agency, Li Yaoliang, the manager of Luochun Pavilion at No. 283 Zhejiang Road, previously claimed that the monthly rent of 900 taels was not sustainable and requested the landlord, Renji Company, to reduce the rent. The rent was reduced to 700 taels. However, the Municipal Council's house tax was calculated based on an estimated value of 1,000 taels. Although Li Yaoliang explained the situation to the tax collector, Mr. Yao, and the Municipal Council sent personnel to investigate and confirm that it was indeed Luochun Pavilion, and the disaster relief official Hu Tiegen went to the Municipal Council's Tax Office and met with the Westerner Kang Molai, who agreed to calculate the tax based on the actual rent of 700 taels, two checks for the winter and spring taxes of 588 taels were sent to the Tax Office the next day. However, Mr. Kang Molai did not issue the tax receipts, but only wrote two receipts, one for the winter tax of 420 taels and one for the spring tax of 168 taels, and wrote in Western text that Luochun Pavilion was unable to pay in full, and only received 168 taels. After negotiating with him, Mr. Kang denied his previous statement and claimed that it had to be calculated based on an estimated value of 1,200 taels. If it is calculated based on 900 taels, it can still be corrected. Otherwise, you can sue, etc. Li Yaoliang immediately sent a letter to the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association for assistance. It is said that the association also believes that the municipal tax should be calculated based on the actual rent as a financial principle. It should not be calculated based on the estimated value. Even if you want to increase revenue, you should consider the burden of the taxpayers and not contribute to the increase in rent, which will affect the social economy. Mr. Kang, the tax collector, is particularly inappropriate, so he has sent a letter to the Director-General of the Municipal Council for review.

United Shipping Vessel Seized for Opium 164

The United Shipping Vessel of Jardine Matheson & Co. arrived in Shanghai from the Yangtze River this time. Yesterday morning at 7:30 AM, the vessel arrived at the White Mao Sha River. The United vessel had barge No. 18, which was carrying twelve tons of tung oil. Unexpectedly, a small vessel with a yellow chimney with four soldiers in uniform and wooden pistols on board drove toward the United vessel. When they saw the United vessel, they ordered it to stop. The United vessel did not dare to resist and immediately dropped anchor. The four men jumped into barge No. 18 and searched the middle cabin, finding two sacks of opium smuggled to Shanghai, weighing more than 200 pounds. Because no suspects were found at that time, the opium was taken to the small vessel and sailed away. The United vessel was able to arrive in Shanghai in the afternoon of yesterday.

Weather Report 173

Yesterday at 4:30 PM, the Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast stating that the Yangtze River basin and the coastal area here would be cloudy with possible rain or heavy rain due to a low-pressure system forming in Jiangxi. Northwesterly winds are strong north of Shandong. South of Ma'an Island, the wind is variable. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 64.6 and the lowest was 49.1. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 66.2 and the lowest was 44.8.

Incoming Correspondence

Letter from the Medical Association on the National Medical Institute 174

The Executive Committee of the Chinese Medical Association wrote to the presidents of the five academies regarding the National Medical Institute, saying: "Gentlemen, your achievements are well-known. We have long looked forward to the opportunity to express our accumulated thoughts on the major plans for medicine and health, but have had no chance to visit your esteemed offices. We deeply regret this. Recently, newspapers have been discussing the establishment of the National Medical Institute. Our association believes that this move by the central government not only affects the relationship between old and new medicine, but also greatly impacts academic progress and national thought. We fear that seeds of error sown today will yield erroneous fruit in the future. It is more than a question of a single word being right or wrong and affecting things a thousand miles away. We, the undersigned, believe that you are pillars of the party and the nation, and that your words carry great weight and can correct wrong paths and bring about righteousness. Therefore, we dare to briefly present our humble opinions for your review."

"The proponents of traditional medicine today claim that it has a history of over four thousand years. In fact, from the beginning of humanity, there have been diseases, and the observation and treatment of them are necessary. Therefore, the seeds of medicine must have existed from the earliest times. Long lifespans are common to all humanity around the world, and not only China has a particularly long history. However, before the 19th century, various sciences had not yet reached a high level of sophistication. The functions and changes in the human body were largely based on speculation and guesswork. Therefore, Western Europe had the theory of four humors and three elements, and China had the theory of five elements and six qi. East and West were essentially the same. These were all unevolved hypotheses. China did not have any outstanding or superhuman insights. In modern times, with the rise of science, Western physicians have used the products of scientific evolution as research aids, abandoning appearances and seeking essence, discarding errors and embracing truth. The observation and treatment of diseases have become increasingly accurate. The old and new have been transformed, and this is how we have reached the present day. But China is not like this. It still reveres old theories and adheres to old ways. Therefore, anyone who understands the common laws of human evolution and the path of academic development in the world can clearly see that the process of Chinese medicine in history is similar to that of ancient and medieval Europe, and its position in the world is that of something backward. There are no special or miraculous treasures to be found. This can be asserted. They... proudly call it a unique academic discipline, a study that is peerless in the universe, just as summer insects talk to the well and frogs in a well cling to the limitations of the moment, or exaggerate and spread misinformation, confusing public opinion. Scholars should reject and refute such claims, and not follow blindly and be misled."

"The fallacy of the essence of traditional medicine has been thoroughly exposed by our colleagues for several years. Let us briefly explain it to you again. The books "Ling Shu" and "Su Wen" were falsely attributed to Taoist alchemists of the Warring States period. People in the past have already reached a definitive conclusion. Therefore, Sima Qian said that the words of the hundred schools of thought about the Yellow Emperor were not elegant or refined. Mr. Wei Shen found it difficult to explain them, and the "Tian Yuan Ji Da Lun" and other works are especially similar to the prophecies in the "Wei Shu" of the Qin and Han Dynasties. It is clear evidence that the origins of medicine lie in shamanism. From Zhang Zhongjing down to Cao Yuanfang, Sun Simiao, and Wang Tao, the "Qianjin Fang," "Wai Tai Mi Yao," "Sheng Ji Zong Lu," and "He Hui Fang" recorded diseases and listed prescriptions, gradually moving towards practicality. However, in the late Song Dynasty, the pedantic scholars of Neo-Confucianism viewed the ancient sages and wise kings as omniscient and omnipotent, and revered them as gods. Therefore, the scholars of the Jin and Yuan dynasties specialized in interpreting the "Nei Jing," resulting in obscure and confusing debates. Chinese medicine then followed the wrong path, enduring many tribulations without recovery. During the Ming and Qing dynasties, metaphysical discussions flourished. Occasionally, there were outstanding figures such as Chen Sicheng, the author of "Wei Chuang Mi Lu," and Wang Qingren, the author of "Yi Lin Gai Cuo," who advocated realism and practicality, but few people echoed them. The masses of doctors remained immersed in the debates about yin and yang, qi transformation, and the differentiation between cold, heat, deficiency, and excess, like foolishly building walls and planting weeds. The object of medicine is the biological, flesh-and-blood body. Therefore, there is anatomy to clarify its structure, physiology to study its function, pathology to understand its changes, and pharmacology to remedy its defects. Traditional medicine's anatomy is the viscera and meridians; its physiology is nutrient essence, blood, and qi; its pathology is the five elements and six qi; its pharmacology is cold, heat, warm, and cool. All are vague, general, and seemingly correct but actually false statements, empty theories, carrying a cartload of ghosts, without any practical method of seeking truth from facts, or any firm basis for verification. Because its words lack detail and evidence, they are not credible. Therefore, debates accumulate without any definite conclusion, and there is no progress to speak of after thousands of years. This is the reason. As for its therapeutic achievements, one is attributing the work of nature to oneself. As Yu Quyuan said in "Yi Lun," the medicine that cures is the one that would have cured even without the medicine. The other is the use of facts discovered by human instinct. As Yang Quan said in "Wu Li Lun," rhubarb relieves constipation and angelica stops pain, just as beans and millet relieve hunger and soup and water quench thirst. These are common experiences, and there is no other miraculous effect."

"Those who preside over the National Medical Institute say that they want to modernize traditional medicine. Their intention is good. However, what is called science in modern times, whether natural science or social science, takes the real phenomena of the natural world and the current state of social life as its subject matter. The method of research strictly follows the rules of mathematics, physics, and chemistry, and the laws of logic, and uses the paradigms of statistics to make judgments and determine right and wrong, and does not dare to make absurd and unfounded claims. As for fabricating facts, concocting laws, defining a system, making far-fetched analogies, and manipulating things according to one's own ideas to form one's own school of thought, it is merely fantasy. Witches, blind musicians, astrologers, and ancient philosophers and ancient medicine all belong to this category. From this point of view, it is clear that traditional medicine cannot be classified as science. The seven-foot body and the diseases of all people are all real phenomena of the natural world, and it is also clear that medicine cannot be manipulated according to one's own ideas. Therefore, to study medicine, one must base it on the laws of nature. To modernize traditional medicine, one must have people with scientific knowledge and scientific training to sort it out, in order to be reasonable. If one appoints people who do not understand science to study it, it is like asking blind people to distinguish colors, or deaf people to judge music. Its achievements can be predicted in advance. At best, it can only collect medical theories from the past, arbitrarily select and discard them, mix them with half-understood new empty theories, imitate the "Tu Shu Ji Cheng," and intensify the situation. This is already the best possible achievement. Beyond this, it can be of no use. Yet... they proclaim to the public that they are modernizing it. They say it without shame, and it will be difficult to do. As the poem says, 'Eloquent words flow from the mouth, and clever words are like a tongue. What a thick face!' This is what it means. It is not appropriate for our party to let the people of the whole country be startled by empty words, and it is not appropriate for you, gentlemen, to participate in it." (To be continued)

Incoming Letter 175

To the editor of Shen Bao, I recently read a news item in today's (i.e., March 13th) local news column about Dr. Deng Lanpu, an expert in otolaryngology, opening a clinic. Both are well-known for their ability to extract foreign objects from the trachea and esophagus, but they do not advertise. Sincerely, Sun Yonggao, Qitong Correspondence Office, Weihaiwei Road, March 13th.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom 176

— Held by Buddha

▲ Everyone is a blacksmith forging their own happiness.

▲ Life is like a journey through the desert, with more dryness and less flavor. Hurricanes are demons, and water and grass are love gods. Hurricanes are everywhere, but fertile water and grass are few and far between.

▲ Focus makes change possible. Reading more books by sages and worthies will make you appear dignified. Reading more books by Buddhists and Taoists will make you appear spiritually clear. The clear-minded are intelligent, and the slovenly are vulgar. Observe their person and hear their words, and you will have more than half the answer to choosing friends.

▲ The mind is easily moved, and people are easily drawn to good or evil. Novels, ballads, movies, and dramas have great potential power. I deeply hope that people today will be courageous in creating good and not sowing the seeds of evil.

▲ The power of love is unmatched by any other power. However, this "centripetal force" can be broken down by "centrifugal force." What is centrifugal force? It is reading appropriate books.

▲ Suicide is the act of a coward. Although the universe is narrow, is there no place to eat? Dying in the Arctic is the same as dying in a ditch, but there is a difference between Mount Tai and a feather. People in troubled times must have role models in their minds to encourage themselves and others.

Anecdotes about President Lin Zichao 177

— Li Qingduo

Lin Sen, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee, recently went abroad with Chen Yaoyuan, director of the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, to investigate party affairs and overseas Chinese affairs. Just as they arrived in Little Luzon, President Hu Zhantang resigned, and Lin was ordered to serve as president of the Legislative Yuan. I will briefly describe one or two of Lin's anecdotes, which I believe readers will be happy to know.

Lin Sen, courtesy name Zichao, is from Fujian. In the past, he handled party affairs overseas and supported the revolution, achieving great success and earning the trust of General Sun. Overseas Chinese have deep faith in Lin, and his great name has long been famous overseas and respected at home. His qualifications in the party and the nation are very old.

In 1927, Lin arrived in Shanghai from Minhou and stayed at the East Asia Hotel. One day, I visited him and saw many books in the room. Lin was holding a volume and sitting quietly, reading. When he saw me arrive, he asked me to sit down. After some polite conversation, his friend Deng began talking with me, and Lin went back to reading as before. This shows that Lin is diligent in reading, meticulous in research, and especially cherishes his valuable time.

Lin's private residence in Minhou is in Cangqianshan, with a beautiful and charming landscape. When Lin lives in Beijing and Shanghai, he occasionally takes the time to return to Fujian to rest and enjoy the scenery of his hometown. Jiujiang and Guling are known as summer resorts with elegant scenery, and Lin also likes to visit them. Last year, he went to Guling to escape the summer heat.

Lin is nearly seventy years old. Although his hair is not entirely white, his beard is quite long. He is very energetic and walks briskly. He gets up very early, works tirelessly, and is usually very simple. He often wears a cloth robe, which is like the style of the ancients. His residence in Shanghai only hires one or two servants. His frugality is such.

A Sincere Admonition 178

— Tao Zaidong

The love suicide of Tang and Bai last month is truly a lamentable tragedy of thirty-six lovebirds with a common fate, a pair of pitiful butterflies. Reading their few lines of suicide note, one can see their sincerity. Their relationship must have been filled with many hardships. The true meaning of love, and so on, fills their hearts. Even if they can compete with the sun and moon for glory, I have something to say. Of all living things, the human body is the most precious. The highest are sages and heroes, followed by talented scholars and beautiful women, then famous actors and prostitutes, and finally ordinary husbands and wives. How can one waste the opportunity to be born in the world as decided by Yama, and return empty-handed? I like Zhuangzi's words the most: "The Great Mass carries me with form, labors me with life, eases me with age, and rests me with death. He who loves my life also loves my death." Therefore, avoiding the labor of life and pursuing an unwholesome death is called going against fate. Therefore, religion punishes those who cannot be reborn, and the law considers it a crime. Moreover, suicide has always been called cowardice, and double suicide is even more contrary to morality. If one cannot avoid the storms on the Lan Bridge, or the thorns in the distant Penglai Island, then, as the saying goes, "The higher the Tao, the longer the demon," one should meet the soldiers with generals. It has been said that the person can return three times, and the moon can be seen twice. Youth is no better than the yellow earth where the mandarin ducks lie. Alas, Tang and Bai are gone. What I feel is that all love is like the true meaning of Tang and Bai? Among them, can the utilitarianism, money, romance, song, dance, deformity, and coercion be denied? Therefore, it is common to see poems of fans being rejected in the morning and petitions for divorce in the evening. Moreover, there is the bitterness of the lotus in the heart, the thorns of the rose piercing the hand, and the shadow of the sand cast on the jade, which is difficult to erase. The clouds and rain turn over, the moon falls, and the stars fade. Even if one throws a mouse, one is afraid of breaking the vase, and it is difficult to cut off the head of a viper. The crazy ones swallow pain to kill themselves, and the mad ones are treacherous and romantic. Such foolish men and resentful women suffer in vain, and their karmic debts are difficult to repay. However, for those lost in the labyrinth of realization, there must be a middle path to point the way. I believe that in the years of schooling, it is more important to seek knowledge than to seek a partner. The harm of unrequited love is less than that of losing one's body. Etiquette and education should be interpreted as order, and why must they be overthrown so quickly? Men and women should be friends, and there is plenty of room for inquiry. Avoid the suspicion of throwing pearls into the dark. It does not hurt for matchmakers to introduce, invoking the meaning of the old horse knowing the way. Parents should be consulted, remembering the words of caution at the beginning of marriage, and being mindful of the admonition of assessing character. It is important to comprehensively observe the environment and avoid being childish and learning civilization. Beauty comes from causes, and completion comes from delay. Thus, grievances and resentments are both eliminated through external action, and love is guaranteed its freedom. Otherwise, throwing oneself into the net of love too easily is like binding oneself, only to regret being like a silkworm making its own cocoon. Once the flames of desire ignite, it is difficult to save the moth that rushes to the lamp, only to follow in the footsteps of the moth in the moon palace, adding a page to the history of tragedy. Is this not a cause for grief? This is why I wrote this sincere admonition. May the son of the state and the daughter of the nation not laugh at these humble words. This official is a new entrant and does not shrink from taboos, daring to offend the imperial majesty. I am filled with trepidation.

Note by Juan: Tang is a fellow writer, and Tang Meixi is a young and talented man, gentle and refined, with a foundation in epigraphy, poetry, and fiction. Last year, he attempted suicide at the West Lake Hotel and was rescued. Now, he has finally died for love. Alas, I am saddened.

The Butterfly Board Plays, the Butterfly Powder is Fresh 179

— Lucky Person

Ms. Hu Die has devoted herself to the screen and her reputation has spread, earning widespread praise. I still remember two years ago, when song and dance dramas were popular in Shanghai. The children of the film industry dared not lag behind. When the Mingxing Film Company's "Blood of a Lover" premiered at the Central Grand Theater, all the male and female stars joined in singing the "Great Grape Fairy" on stage. The role of the fairy in the play was played by Hu Die. Her delicate voice turned and twisted, and those who heard it listened attentively. Her teacher, Mr. Wang Meiyu, praised her as a rare talent and composed a song to promote her, with the line, "The Hu family's charming daughter is named Hu Die. The butterfly board plays, the butterfly powder is fresh." The teacher once listened to songs for forty years and rarely praised anyone. Ms. Hu's oriole voice is graceful and can be heard for three days, but unfortunately, only those near the water tower can taste it. If it could be recorded and shown with the film, then two beauties would be combined into one. Now, years have passed, and the sound film "Sing-song Girl Red Peony" is popular far and wide, and the starring role is played by Ms. Hu. Mr. Wang can be said to be a connoisseur.

Trivial News from the Xin Chang Incident 180

— Facts

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Chang ship hit a reef, resulting in a loss of more than one million yuan, which is a great misfortune. The details have already been reported in the newspapers. Here are some small news items about this incident:

▲ Stranded on a Warship: The Xin Chang hit a reef six or seven li from Ma'an Mountain and one li from Sijiao Mountain, between Huanglong Mountain and Dingshan, a place called Arite Reef. It is located in the middle of the four mountains. First, the bow of the ship became trapped in the reef, and then the engine room broke and all the lights went out. Decades ago, China's first cruiser, the Hai Tian (even larger than the Hai Qi), sank in the same place. Now, the Xin Chang accident occurred on top of the sunken body of the Hai Tian warship. The Xin Chang's draft was eighteen feet, and the bottom of the ship was supported by the Hai Tian's chimney and pilot platform. The reason it could last a day and a night without sinking was the lifting force of the Hai Tian. Until forty-eight hours later, the bow of the ship began to enter the sea, the cabin broke, and the whole ship sank, with only one chimney exposed on the surface of the sea.

▲ All Crew Members Drifting at Sea: After the accident, Tang Rihua and the other twenty-five employees of the cargo department first released four wooden planks into the sea to escape. The danger of navigating in the dark on a lonely boat amidst the stormy waves can be imagined. Unexpectedly, the wooden planks were not equipped with oars. The twenty-five people were tossed by the waves and could not control themselves, so they let them drift with the waves on the sea. At the critical moment, the Yihua Guangsheng ship arrived and the shipowner discovered them and tried hard to salvage them, and all twenty-five people were saved.

▲ Bald Heads and Bare Feet: The ship hit the reef at 7:05 AM, and the lights went out at 9:00 AM. There were a total of 112 workers on the ship. At that time, they only wanted to survive, and rushed to the deck to grab the lifeboats. At that time, those who lost their shoes and hats did not care. Some had already entered the cabin and were preparing to sleep, but got up in a hurry and did not even have time to put on their clothes. They escaped to Arite Island and Sijiao Mountain in four batches. They starved on the mountain for twenty-four hours, and most of them were in thin clothes, suffering from hunger and cold. Their misery was unbearable. When they arrived in Shanghai, they were extremely embarrassed. The Bureau has agreed to give each person forty yuan as a subsidy.

▲ The Huge Loss: The Xin Chang was the first ocean liner of China Merchants, and its steel hull was of the highest quality, worth 800,000 taels. The Hong Kong government's ship inspections are the strictest. Ships that are slightly old are not allowed to travel. Those that are allowed to carry passengers to Hong Kong must be special first-class ships. The Xin Chang was one that could carry passengers to Hong Kong, so its quality can be known. The quality of its machinery was especially the best. This time, just in terms of freight costs, the loss is about 200,000 yuan. Combined with the value of the ship's body, the crew's belongings, and passengers' luggage, the loss is about 1.3 million yuan.

▲ Books Also Looted: After the shipwreck, fishing boats considered it the only benefit they should enjoy. The day after the Xin Chang hit the reef, four fishing boats sailed to the ship and looted all the public and private property and money. Moreover, they looted the various foreign books specially prepared in the shipowner's office, the first-class cabin, the account books in the accounting room, and the special and valuable navigational charts used by the shipowner and the first and second mates. If the navy is not sent to protect them, I am afraid that the engine and machinery will also be dismantled.

Spring in the Art World 181

— Zheng Yimei

"A year's plan starts in spring." This is the clear teaching of the ancients. The members of the Yicheng Society are working hard in spring, and therefore a spring painting and calligraphy exhibition is being held. Yu Guang's writing of mountains, red trees, small boats, and stone bridges is faint in meaning and majestic in atmosphere, which belongs to fine works. Wang Ziyuan's landscape with colors is intended to be between Da Chi and Lu Tai, and is also a work that is only worth watching. Jiang Yinan's plum blossoms in ink and vermilion are unique in charm, and he sends a branch of spring to Jiangnan. He is worthy of his name. Li Qiyun is old in revolution. He was lucky enough to escape from the Huanghuagang uprising. Recently, he has been living by the seaside and often uses painting to express the depression in his heart. He hangs several works on the wall. His brushwork is wonderful and does not adhere to the rules. If you judge by the standards of the law, you are not a friend of Qiyun. Qiyun's signature is "Qingxiang Old Man." Meng Shouzhi's painting of vegetables is lifelike and can fill a plate. In winter, the cold is bitter and the vegetables are damaged by frost, and the price is strangely high. Although we poor scholars want to bite the roots of vegetables, it is very difficult. Looking at it, one cannot help but drool. Qian Hufo's Buddha has been found outside the room since Zhao Yiqian, and is becoming more and more refined and healthy. Wu Shigong's flowers and plants have the artistic style of Dong Xin. In terms of calligraphy, there are Yang Xizi, Luo Lianggong, and Xiong Jizhen, who are quite lively. After appreciating it, I had a meeting with Hufo and Mr. Yuan Xilian. Mr. Yuan has recently devoted himself to meditation and is able to personally write Brahma scriptures, release flames alone, and eliminate evil. A few days ago, Yao Minghui built the Amitabha Pagoda in Jinsu Town, An'ting, and invited Mr. Yuan to chant scriptures. Farmers came to watch, so they invited a photographer to take a picture as a souvenir. In the picture, a mountain emerged behind the pagoda. There are no hills within two hundred miles of An'ting, so it was considered a miracle. The photo was shown to Mr. Yuan, and indeed there was a faint shape of undulating hills. Everyone was surprised for a long time. Hufo collected cigarette boxes, which are very rich, and intends to hold an exhibition, showing dozens or hundreds of them, all of which are famous and precious. It is said that the Beauty brand originally had the words "Lu Meiyu," but after a dispute, the three words were removed. Also, the Zun brand originally had the card pattern of "Yao Ding Er Si," and some said that it promoted gambling, so it was changed to "Seven Stars." The Fairy brand fairy holds a five-color flag. Since the Party army cleared the territory, the five-color flag has been transformed into a shield. New images are common and the old view cannot be seen again. It is currently being sought. Unexpectedly, a small box has such vicissitudes. However, those who are not as mindful as Hufo cannot know the details.

Heart's Warmth (383) 182

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Seventeen: Secret Art to Preserve Youthful Looks, Emerald Green Dyes the Eyebrows; No Method to Prolong Life, Gold Market for the Swift Steed's Bones

That Auntie Jin was a person without any opinions of her own. Upon hearing that the illness could be contagious, she was initially terrified and then said, "When the Third Young Master and Sixth Young Miss go to the hospital, who will serve them?" Ye San replied, "Didn't I say that there are nurses in the hospital? You don't need to go. Just check on them once a day. Go and call Big Belly Jin in here for me; I have something to say to her." Soon, Big Belly Jin came in, carrying her big belly. She recognized Ye Tonghou and said, "The Third Young Master and Sixth Young Miss, looking at their health, they seemed quite robust. Who knew they would suddenly fall ill?" Ye San then directly said that she had a severe case of diphtheria and would be sent to the hospital tomorrow morning. Big Belly Jin said, "Oh dear, hospitals are very expensive; I'm afraid it will cost several dollars a day!" Seeing Big Belly Jin's hesitation, Ye Tonghou, fearing he would have to take responsibility, said, "You don't have to worry about the hospital fees; I'll take care of the bills." Upon hearing that Ye San would cover the hospital expenses, Big Belly Jin felt relieved of responsibility and knew that the disease was contagious, and there were many young women in the troupe; if it were to spread, it wouldn't be a joke. Another thing that Big Belly Jin was very worried about was that everyone knew diphtheria was contagious, and if this news spread, customers would be too scared to come and watch the shows, which would greatly affect her business. She then immediately agreed. As for the Flower Old Sixth side, Ye San also delicately explained to her. Hua Yuanchun said, "Third Young Master, I'm afraid I'm really going to die in Beijing. Rather than die in the troupe, it's better to die in the hospital. Before leaving, I said in Shanghai that I would treat you as family when I arrived in Beijing, and now you truly are my family." Ye Tonghou said, "Old Sixth, don't say such things. Illness and suffering are just unfortunate times; there's nothing to be surprised about. We are both from the south, and we should help each other. If I were sick, perhaps you would come and take care of me." The next morning, Flower Old Sixth entered the Chengnan Hospital. As she left, she shed a few tears and said, "This time, I'm going to kick the bucket." Auntie Jin could only watch the house in the courtyard and run to the Chengnan Hospital every day to check on her. Ye Tonghou was very busy but still went to see her twice. However, this was an isolation ward, and the doctor was very reluctant for people to visit, so he could only make phone calls to inquire. However, on the seventh day after entering the hospital, Flower Old Sixth's condition was hopeless. Fortunately, Ye Tonghou had not yet left Beijing, so all the clothing and coffin costs were covered by Ye San. Although Flower Old Sixth had some jewelry, Big Belly Jin said that she would keep it safe, fearing it would be lost, since Sixth Miss was not around. It was likely that Old Sixth owed them some money. Ye San also sent a telegram to Grandma Pan in Shanghai, which he had known beforehand. He had asked Flower Old Sixth who her best girlfriend in Shanghai was, and she said it was Grandma Pan.

Standard Gold Shows Signs of Weakness 183

Fluctuations occurred from time to time. Yesterday, March 14th, the trend of standard gold showed weakness. In the morning, it was sluggish, and then suddenly, three or four taels of trading volume fluctuated inexplicably. Eventually, it continued to fall by four taels, breaking the 700-tael mark. The foreign exchange rate lengthened by half a point, while the domestic market turned weak to flat. The overseas silver market rose slightly, but the situation was peaceful, so the gold price was not affected. Trading within the market was still active, with Dalian gangs, Yuansheng, Xinheng, Hengxing, Yuan Fuchang, etc., all buying in, and Zhifeng, Yongqian, Changxiang, etc., having frequent transactions. Fuyu, Hongli, Hengyu, etc., were sellers. Soon after, bills of exchange became loose, leading to a downfall of ten taels, especially with swaps approaching, requiring more parties to post bonds, resulting in scattered floating and some selling. Furthermore, with strong buying momentum and British gold banks still accommodating at 1 shilling and 4 pence to 3 pence 9375, the gold price gradually rose, and the atmosphere turned peaceful. Finally, it stood at over 697 taels. In the afternoon, due to the Saturday market closure, the week's turbulent and unpredictable nature was traced back. The highest price was 746 taels and 8 mace, and the lowest price reached 683 taels and 3 mace, with a difference of 63 taels and 5 mace. Overall, it suddenly fell by 45 taels, which is considered significant.

A decrease of 3 taels and 7 mace occurred from the morning's April opening at 701 taels and a half, the same as yesterday's closing. The silver price rose slightly by one-sixteenth, adding eight and three-eighths of a cent. The initial telegraph only added one-sixteenth, and people's hearts stabilized. Wanxing and others bought in, causing a brief rise of 0.04 taels, but it quickly turned downward, with Fuyu, Hengyu, Yuancheng, Yongyuan, Maoyong, etc., selling off. There were also rumors of the Japanese Hamaguchi cabinet resigning, creating a troubled atmosphere that led to a sharp drop of over 11 taels, reaching 692 taels and 5 mace. Soon after, there were slightly more buyers, increasing to 95 taels and 5 mace, but British gold became even more scarce. Banks advanced from 1.39375 to 4 pence, then 4 pence could be settled, which was then bought by Shanghai for next month at .0625. With Dachengsheng and Richang eager to sell, at 9:28, it suddenly rose by over 4 taels to 95 taels when the quotation of 90 taels and 0.05 shillings was revealed. The listing lengthened by 0.125. U.S. gold fell by 1.5 cents, settling at 93 taels. Afterwards, Mitsui and Datong bought in for June at 4 pence to 3 pence 9375. Fuchang, Yuanheng, Tongtaichang, Yuancheng, etc., all chased after the purchase, reaching a high point of over 99 taels at 9:50. Hongli and others sold off, momentarily retreating by over 4 taels. At 10:00, it was 94 taels and 5 mace. Shortly after, Tongtaichang and the Dalian gang sold off. Jardine Matheson and HSBC absorbed it at 3 pence 9375 for April and May, so it rose to 99 taels and a half. After 10:30, softening signs reappeared, with Zhifengyong and hedging selling off, causing a drop of 6 taels. However, at times, there were fluctuations of 2 taels. At 11:00, it was only 93 taels. Subsequently, Qianchangxiang, Shunli, Wanxing, and Yuanheng, etc., advanced, and Tongtaichang also bought in. With British gold sellable at 9375, people's hearts recovered, jumping 7 taels. Futures Wheat Market Rebounds 193

After the opening of the futures wheat market yesterday morning, the market for each month generally showed a flat and weak trend. The price of foreign wheat had been as low as three or four cents, and people inside and outside the industry inevitably turned weak. Although the trend was not good, the minds of those outside the industry were consistently bullish. Those who shorted would never release their positions without determining the price of foreign wheat. The stagnation of the market atmosphere was due to this. Until the afternoon, each month rebounded because the flour market turned stable, and buyers from outside the industry and some floating shorts also started to scramble to cover their positions. Therefore, both the near and far terms saw a rebound. However, since the road to foreign wheat from abroad has not been cut off, there is no time to expect too much.
